RJ-58 (Salumber)</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Nearest cities</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Bhilwara" title="Bhilwara">Bhilwara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pindwara" title="Pindwara">Pindwara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jodhpur" title="Jodhpur">Jodhpur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chittorgarh" title="Chittorgarh">Chittorgarh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kota,_Rajasthan" title="Kota, Rajasthan">Kota</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ahmedabad" title="Ahmedabad">Ahmedabad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jaipur" title="Jaipur">Jaipur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ajmer" title="Ajmer">Ajmer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indore" title="Indore">Indore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dungarpur" title="Dungarpur">Dungarpur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Banswara" title="Banswara">Banswara</a></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Climate</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate#Hot_semi-arid_climates" title="Semi-arid climate">BSh</a></td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.udaipur.rajasthan.gov.in">www<wbr />.udaipur<wbr />.rajasthan<wbr />.gov<wbr />.in</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Udaipur</b> (<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Udaipur.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a6/Udaipur.ogg" class="internal" title="Udaipur.ogg">pronunciation</a></span>&#160;<small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>·<a href="/wiki/File:Udaipur.ogg" title="File:Udaipur.ogg"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span>) (<a href="/wiki/ISO_15919" title="ISO 15919">ISO 15919</a>: <i>Udayapura</i>) is a <a href="/wiki/City" title="City">city</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipal_corporation_(India)" title="Municipal corporation (India)">municipal corporation</a> in <a href="/wiki/Udaipur_district" title="Udaipur district">Udaipur district</a> of the state of <a href="/wiki/Rajasthan" title="Rajasthan">Rajasthan</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Udaipur_location_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Udaipur_location-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> it is also known as the ''City of Lakes''.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> It is the administrative headquarter of <a href="/wiki/Udaipur_district" title="Udaipur district">Udaipur district</a>. It is the historic capital of the kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Mewar" title="Mewar">Mewar</a> in the  former <a href="/wiki/Rajputana_Agency" title="Rajputana Agency">Rajputana Agency</a>. It was founded in 1559 by <a href="/wiki/Udai_Singh_II" title="Udai Singh II">Udai Singh II</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Sisodia" class="mw-redirect" title="Sisodia">Sisodia</a> clan of <a href="/wiki/Rajput" title="Rajput">Rajputs</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Udaipur_history_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Udaipur_history-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> when he shifted his capital from the city of <a href="/wiki/Chittorgarh" title="Chittorgarh">Chittorgarh</a> to Udaipur after Chittorgarh was besieged by <a href="/wiki/Akbar" title="Akbar">Akbar</a>. It remained as the capital city till 1818 when it became a <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British princely state</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Udaipur_history_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Udaipur_history-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> and thereafter the Mewar province became a part of Rajasthan when India gained <a href="/wiki/Indian_Independence_Act_1947" title="Indian Independence Act 1947">independence</a> in 1947.<sup id="cite_ref-udaipur.org.uk_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-udaipur.org.uk-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The city is located in the southernmost part of Rajasthan, near the <a href="/wiki/Gujarat" title="Gujarat">Gujarat</a> border. It is surrounded by the <a href="/wiki/Aravali_Range" class="mw-redirect" title="Aravali Range">Aravali Range</a>, which separates it from the <a href="/wiki/Thar_Desert" title="Thar Desert">Thar Desert</a>. It is placed almost in the middle of two major Indian metro cities, around 660&#160;km from <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a> and 800&#160;km from <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>. Besides, connectivity with <a href="/wiki/Gujarat" title="Gujarat">Gujarat</a> ports provide Udaipur a strategic geographical advantage.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Udaipur is well connected with nearby cities and states by means of road, rail and air transportation facilities. The city is served by the <a href="/wiki/Maharana_Pratap_Airport" title="Maharana Pratap Airport">Maharana Pratap Airport</a>. Common languages spoken include <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rajasthani_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Rajasthani language">Rajasthani</a> (<a href="/wiki/Mewari_language" title="Mewari language">Mewari</a>).
</p><p>Dubbed "the most romantic spot on the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">continent of India</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Company_rule_in_India" title="Company rule in India">British</a> administrator <a href="/wiki/James_Tod" title="James Tod">James Tod</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Udaipur is a tourist destination and is known for its history, culture, scenic locations and the Rajput-era palaces. It has seven lakes surrounding the city. <a href="/wiki/Udaipur_City%27s_Five_lakes" title="Udaipur City&#39;s Five lakes">Five</a> of the major lakes, namely <a href="/wiki/Fateh_Sagar_Lake" title="Fateh Sagar Lake">Fateh Sagar Lake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Pichola" title="Lake Pichola">Lake Pichola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swaroop_Sagar_Lake" title="Swaroop Sagar Lake">Swaroop Sagar Lake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rang_Sagar_Lake" title="Rang Sagar Lake">Rangsagar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Doodh_Talai_Lake" title="Doodh Talai Lake">Doodh Talai Lake</a>, have been included under the restoration project of the National Lake Conservation Plan (NLCP) of the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">Government of India</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NLCP_Report_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NLCP_Report-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Besides lakes, Udaipur is also known for its historic forts and palaces, museums, galleries, natural locations and gardens, architectural temples, as well as traditional fairs, festivals and structures.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Due to the several lakes present here, it is sometimes dubbed "<i><a href="/wiki/Venice_of_the_East" title="Venice of the East">Venice of the East</a></i>".<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Udaipur economy is primarily driven by tourism, though minerals, marble processing, chemical manufacturing and development, electronic manufacturing and the handicraft industry are also contributors.<sup id="cite_ref-economy_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economy-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Udaipur hosts several state and regional public offices, including offices of Director of Mines and Geology, Commissioner of Excise, Commissioner of Tribal Area Development, <a href="/wiki/Hindustan_Zinc" title="Hindustan Zinc">Hindustan Zinc Limited</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rajasthan_State_Mines_and_Minerals" title="Rajasthan State Mines and Minerals">Rajasthan State Mines and Mineral Corporation Limited</a>. Besides, Udaipur is rising as educational hub as well, with 5 Universities, 14 colleges and more than 160 high schools.<sup id="cite_ref-economy_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economy-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Udaipur is home to <a href="/wiki/Indian_Institute_of_Management_Udaipur" title="Indian Institute of Management Udaipur">IIM Udaipur</a>, the fifth best management institution in the country according to NIRF ranking released by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Human_Resource_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Human Resource Development">MHRD</a>.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Udaipur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Udaipur_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Udaipur State">Udaipur State</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Udaipur" title="History of Udaipur">History of Udaipur</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistoric_Era">Prehistoric Era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Udaipur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Prehistoric Era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ahar_River" title="Ahar River">Ahar River</a> bank was inhabited in about 2000 BCE. There are footprints of two different civilizations, which provides claims about earliest inhabitants of the Ahar culture: the first ones are the <a href="/wiki/Bhil_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Bhil people">Bhil</a>/Bheels, the indigenous tribes originated at this place, and are still residing in the area in large numbers. The second footprints were of <a href="/wiki/Rajput" title="Rajput">Rajputs</a>, who once entered the enclosed valley, and then continued to live in this place for centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-Udaipurtimes_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Udaipurtimes-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Establishment_as_a_city">Establishment as a city</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Udaipur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Establishment as a city">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Statue_of_Maharana_Pratap_of_Mewar,_commemorating_the_Battle_of_Haldighati,_City_Palace,_Udaipur.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Statue_of_Maharana_Pratap_of_Mewar%2C_commemorating_the_Battle_of_Haldighati%2C_City_Palace%2C_Udaipur.jpg/200px-Statue_of_Maharana_Pratap_of_Mewar%2C_commemorating_the_Battle_of_Haldighati%2C_City_Palace%2C_Udaipur.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="267" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Statue_of_Maharana_Pratap_of_Mewar%2C_commemorating_the_Battle_of_Haldighati%2C_City_Palace%2C_Udaipur.jpg/300px-Statue_of_Maharana_Pratap_of_Mewar%2C_commemorating_the_Battle_of_Haldighati%2C_City_Palace%2C_Udaipur.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Statue_of_Maharana_Pratap_of_Mewar%2C_commemorating_the_Battle_of_Haldighati%2C_City_Palace%2C_Udaipur.jpg/400px-Statue_of_Maharana_Pratap_of_Mewar%2C_commemorating_the_Battle_of_Haldighati%2C_City_Palace%2C_Udaipur.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1600" /></a><figcaption>Statue of <a href="/wiki/Maharana_Pratap" title="Maharana Pratap">Maharana Pratap</a> of Mewar, commemorating the Battle of Haldighati.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Udaipur was founded in 1559,<sup id="cite_ref-Udaipur_history_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Udaipur_history-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> by Maharana <a href="/wiki/Udai_Singh_II" title="Udai Singh II">Udai Singh II</a> in the fertile circular Girwa Valley to the southwest of <a href="/wiki/Nagda" title="Nagda">Nagda</a>, on the <a href="/wiki/Banas_River" title="Banas River">Banas River</a>. The city was established as the new capital of the <a href="/wiki/Udaipur_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Udaipur State">Mewar kingdom</a>. This area already had a thriving trading town, Ayad, which had served as the capital of Mewar in the 10th through 12th centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-Udaipur_history_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Udaipur_history-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The Girwa region was thus already well known to Chittaud rulers who moved to it whenever the vulnerable tableland Chittaurgarh was threatened with enemy attacks. Rana Udai Singh II, in the wake of 16th-century emergence of artillery warfare, decided during his exile at <a href="/wiki/Kumbhalgarh" title="Kumbhalgarh">Kumbhalgarh</a> to move his capital to a more secure location. Ayad was flood-prone, hence he chose the ridge east of Pichola Lake to start his new capital city, where he came upon a <a href="/wiki/Hermit" title="Hermit">hermit</a> while hunting in the foothills of the <a href="/wiki/Aravalli_Range" title="Aravalli Range">Aravalli Range</a>. In the myth, the hermit blessed the king and guided him to build a palace on the spot, assuring him it would be well protected. Udai Singh II consequently established a residence on the site. In November 1567, the <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Emperor" class="mw-redirect" title="Mughal Emperor">Mughal Emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Akbar" title="Akbar">Akbar</a> <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Chittorgarh_(1567%E2%80%931568)" title="Siege of Chittorgarh (1567–1568)">conquered Chittor</a>. To protect his territory from attack, Rana Udai Singh built a six-kilometre-long city wall, with seven gates,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> namely <a href="/wiki/Surajpole_(Udaipur)" title="Surajpole (Udaipur)">Surajpole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chandpole_(Udaipur)" title="Chandpole (Udaipur)">Chandpole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Udiapole" title="Udiapole">Udiapole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hathipole_(Udaipur)" title="Hathipole (Udaipur)">Hathipole</a>, Ambapole, Brahmpole, Delhi Gate, and Kishanpole. The area within these walls and gates is still known as the old city or the walled city.
</p><p>In September 1576, <a href="/wiki/Akbar" title="Akbar">Akbar</a> himself arrived at Udaipur and remained there for 6 months until May 1577.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> In 1615, Rana Amar Singh accepted vassalship to Mughal rule under Emperor <a href="/wiki/Jahangir" title="Jahangir">Jahangir</a> and Udaipur remained the capital of the state, which became a <a href="/wiki/Princely_state" title="Princely state">princely state</a> of <a href="/wiki/British_India" class="mw-redirect" title="British India">British India</a> in 1818. Being a mountainous region and unsuitable for heavily armoured Mughal horses, Udaipur remained safe from Mughal influence despite much pressure.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> At present, <a href="/wiki/Maharana" title="Maharana">Maharana</a> <a href="/wiki/Mahendra_Singh_Mewar" title="Mahendra Singh Mewar">Mahendra Singh Mewar</a>  is the 76th custodian of the Mewar dynasty.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Udaipur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jharmar_Kotra_national_geological_monument">Jharmar Kotra national geological monument</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Udaipur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Jharmar Kotra national geological monument">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><span class="anchor" id="Jharmar_Kotra_Stromatolite_Fossil_Park"></span>
Jharmar Kotra Stromatolite Fossil Park at Jharmar Kotra south-east of Udaipur has been declared the <a href="/wiki/List_of_National_Geological_Monuments_in_India" class="mw-redirect" title="List of National Geological Monuments in India">National Geological Monuments of India</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Geological_Survey_of_India" title="Geological Survey of India">Geological Survey of India</a> (GSI), for their protection, maintenance, promotion and enhancement of <a href="/wiki/Geotourism" title="Geotourism">geotourism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gsi1_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gsi1-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gsi2_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gsi2-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gsi3_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gsi3-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gossan_in_Rajpura-Dariba_Mineralised_belt">Gossan in Rajpura-Dariba Mineralised belt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Udaipur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Gossan in Rajpura-Dariba Mineralised belt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><span class="anchor" id="Gossan_in_Rajpura-Dariba_Mineralised_belt"></span>
Gossan in Rajpura-Dariba Mineralised belt nearby, consisting of <a href="/wiki/Gossan" title="Gossan">gossan</a>, has been declared the <a href="/wiki/List_of_National_Geological_Monuments_in_India" class="mw-redirect" title="List of National Geological Monuments in India">National Geological Monuments of India</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Geological_Survey_of_India" title="Geological Survey of India">Geological Survey of India</a> (GSI), for their protection, maintenance, promotion and enhancement of <a href="/wiki/Geotourism" title="Geotourism">geotourism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gsi1_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gsi1-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gsi2_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gsi2-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gsi3_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gsi3-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Topography">Topography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Udaipur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Topography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-halign-center" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:India_-_Udaipur_-_001_-_Udaipur_Palace_panorama_from_the_lake_(1038245526).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/India_-_Udaipur_-_001_-_Udaipur_Palace_panorama_from_the_lake_%281038245526%29.jpg/800px-India_-_Udaipur_-_001_-_Udaipur_Palace_panorama_from_the_lake_%281038245526%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="800" height="275" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/India_-_Udaipur_-_001_-_Udaipur_Palace_panorama_from_the_lake_%281038245526%29.jpg/1200px-India_-_Udaipur_-_001_-_Udaipur_Palace_panorama_from_the_lake_%281038245526%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/India_-_Udaipur_-_001_-_Udaipur_Palace_panorama_from_the_lake_%281038245526%29.jpg/1600px-India_-_Udaipur_-_001_-_Udaipur_Palace_panorama_from_the_lake_%281038245526%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5370" data-file-height="1847" /></a><figcaption><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">The <a href="/wiki/City_Palace,_Udaipur" title="City Palace, Udaipur">City Palace</a> alongside <a href="/wiki/Lake_Pichola" title="Lake Pichola">Lake Pichola</a>.</div></figcaption></figure>
<p>Udaipur is located at <span class="geo-inline"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1156832818"><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Udaipur&amp;params=24.525049_N_73.677116_E_"><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">24°31′30″N</span> <span class="longitude">73°40′38″E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">24.525049°N 73.677116°E</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">24.525049; 73.677116</span></span></span></a></span></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The city covers an area of 64&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (25&#160;sq&#160;mi)<sup id="cite_ref-JanaaGraha_Udaipur_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JanaaGraha_Udaipur-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> and lies at an altitude of 598.00&#160;m (1,962&#160;ft) above sea level. It is located in the southern region of Rajasthan, near the <a href="/wiki/Gujarat" title="Gujarat">Gujarat</a> border.<sup id="cite_ref-Udaipur_location_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Udaipur_location-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The city lies 403&#160;km (250&#160;mi) southwest of the state capital, <a href="/wiki/Jaipur" title="Jaipur">Jaipur</a> and 250&#160;km (155&#160;mi) northeast from <a href="/wiki/Ahmedabad" title="Ahmedabad">Ahmedabad</a>.
</p><p>Udaipur with its lakes lies on the south slope of the <a href="/wiki/Aravalli_Range" title="Aravalli Range">Aravalli Range</a> in Rajasthan. The northern part of the district consists generally of elevated plateaus, while the eastern part has vast stretches of fertile plains. The southern part is covered with rocks, Hills and dense Forest. There are two important passages in the Aravali ranges viz. <a href="/wiki/Desuri" title="Desuri">Desuri</a> Nal and Saoke which serves as a link between Udaipur and <a href="/wiki/Jodhpur_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Jodhpur District">Jodhpur District</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dcmsme_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dcmsme-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The lakes of the city being interconnected form a lake system which supports and sustains the groundwater recharge, water availability for drinking, agriculture, industries and is a source of employment through tourism. The lake system has three main lakes in its upper catchment area, six lakes within its municipal boundary and one lake in the downstream. The Udaipur lake system, arising out of the river Berach (Banas Basin) and its tributaries, is an integral component of the upper Berach basin. The upper Berach basin is a part of the Gangetic river system, wherein the river Berach meets river <a href="/wiki/Ganga" class="mw-redirect" title="Ganga">Ganga</a> through the rivers <a href="/wiki/Banas_River" title="Banas River">Banas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chambal_River" title="Chambal River">Chambal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yamuna" title="Yamuna">Yamuna</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-udaipur_lakes_and_ecology_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-udaipur_lakes_and_ecology-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Udaipur Lake System can be divided into the following categories:<sup id="cite_ref-udaipur_lakes_and_ecology_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-udaipur_lakes_and_ecology-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Upper lakes: <a href="/wiki/Lake_Badi" title="Lake Badi">Lake Badi</a>, Chhota Madar and Bada Madar</li>
<li>City Lakes: <a href="/wiki/Lake_Pichola" title="Lake Pichola">Lake Pichola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fateh_Sagar_Lake" title="Fateh Sagar Lake">Fateh Sagar Lake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swaroop_Sagar_Lake" title="Swaroop Sagar Lake">Swaroop Sagar Lake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rang_Sagar_Lake" title="Rang Sagar Lake">Rang Sagar</a>, Kumharia Talab, Goverdhan Sagar.</li>
<li>Downstream Lake: <a href="/wiki/Udaisagar_Lake" title="Udaisagar Lake">Udaisagar Lake</a></li>
<li>River: <a href="/wiki/Ahar_River" title="Ahar River">Ayad River</a></li></ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Udaipur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-halign-center" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Panoroma_of_Old_City_od_Udaipur.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Panoroma_of_Old_City_od_Udaipur.jpg/800px-Panoroma_of_Old_City_od_Udaipur.jpg" decoding="async" width="800" height="152" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Panoroma_of_Old_City_od_Udaipur.jpg/1200px-Panoroma_of_Old_City_od_Udaipur.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Panoroma_of_Old_City_od_Udaipur.jpg/1600px-Panoroma_of_Old_City_od_Udaipur.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1939" data-file-height="368" /></a><figcaption><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">Panoramic view of old city of Udaipur with City Palace behind it.</div></figcaption></figure>
<p>Udaipur city has a hot <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">semi-arid climate</a>. The three main seasons, summer, monsoon and winter respectively, dominate the city of Udaipur. Being located in the desert lands of Rajasthan, the climate and weather of Udaipur is usually hot. The summer season runs from mid-March to June and touches temperature ranging from 23&#160;°C (73&#160;°F) to 44&#160;°C (111&#160;°F) in the months of March to June.  Monsoons arrive in the month of July heralded by dust and thunderstorms.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> With its greenery and lakes, the city is one of the top monsoon destinations of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The winter season prevails from the month of October till the month of March. Humidity, which prevails during monsoons, diminishes at the arrival of winters. The city observes pleasant sunny days and enjoyable cool nights with the temperature ranging from 5&#160;°C (41&#160;°F) to 30&#160;°C (86&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Udaipur's monsoon and winter climates are the most appealing time to visit. Tourists arrive in large numbers, anytime between mid-September to late March or early April. Even in January, the coldest month, the days are bright, sunny and warm with maximum temperature around 28.3&#160;°C (82.9&#160;°F). Mornings, evenings and nights are cold.<sup id="cite_ref-tourism_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tourism-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<p>According to the 2011 census, the total population of Udaipur city was 451,100. Including suburbs outside the city limits the population was 474,531.<sup id="cite_ref-c2011_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-c2011-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> As per the data, the male population of the city was 233,959 and the female population was 217,141 in 2011. The total population for the age group of 0–6 years old was 47,932. The sex-ratio of the city was 928. The child sex-ratio (0–6 years of age) was 866.
</p><p>As per the estimated 2019 population data, the total population of Udaipur is 662,992.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> In recent years, the population growth of Udaipur has increased amazingly due to its weather, relaxing environment and wonderful places to visit nearby.
</p><p>Udaipur has an average effective literacy rate of 90.43 percent, as compared to the national average of 74.04 percent:<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> male literacy rate being 95.41 percent while the female literacy rate being 85.08 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mewari" class="mw-redirect" title="Mewari">Mewari</a> are the major languages spoken in Udaipur. <a href="/wiki/Marwari_language" title="Marwari language">Marwari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wagdi_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Wagdi language">Wagdi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gujarati_language" title="Gujarati language">Gujarati</a> are some others which are in use in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> is the major religion followed in the city, with 72.9% of the city's population being <a href="/wiki/Hindu" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu">Hindu</a>. <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a> come second at 15.6%. The city also has a large Jain community. <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jains</a> makes about 10% of the population of Udaipur, as compared to the <a href="/wiki/2011_Census_of_India" title="2011 Census of India">national average</a> of 0.37%.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Udaipur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Udaipur_Municipal_Corporation" title="Udaipur Municipal Corporation">Udaipur Municipal Corporation</a></div>
<p>Udaipur is governed by the <a href="/wiki/Udaipur_Municipal_Corporation" title="Udaipur Municipal Corporation">Udaipur Municipal Corporation</a>. The corporation has 70 municipal wards and Govind Singh Tak is the mayor. The city had a city council that was converted into a municipal corporation in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Recently, an all-woman police patrol team was deployed in Udaipur. The initiative, taken by the Rajasthan government, is aimed at ensuring the security of women from eve-teasers, and for the general safety of the public, especially tourists. The team is fully equipped with arms, security equipment, first aid and other amenities besides motorcycles for patrolling the city.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Udaipur_(Lok_Sabha_constituency)" class="mw-redirect" title="Udaipur (Lok Sabha constituency)">Udaipur</a> has its own constituency for representation in the <a href="/wiki/Lok_Sabha" title="Lok Sabha">Lok Sabha</a>. The current representative of Udaipur is <a href="/wiki/Arjunlal_Meena" title="Arjunlal Meena">Arjunlal Meena</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Bharatiya_Janata_Party" title="Bharatiya Janata Party">BJP</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Udaipur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Durbar_Hall,_Fateh_Prakash_Palace_Hotel,_Udaipur.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Durbar_Hall%2C_Fateh_Prakash_Palace_Hotel%2C_Udaipur.jpg/220px-Durbar_Hall%2C_Fateh_Prakash_Palace_Hotel%2C_Udaipur.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Durbar_Hall%2C_Fateh_Prakash_Palace_Hotel%2C_Udaipur.jpg/330px-Durbar_Hall%2C_Fateh_Prakash_Palace_Hotel%2C_Udaipur.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Durbar_Hall%2C_Fateh_Prakash_Palace_Hotel%2C_Udaipur.jpg/440px-Durbar_Hall%2C_Fateh_Prakash_Palace_Hotel%2C_Udaipur.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4272" data-file-height="2848" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/Durbar_Hall" class="mw-redirect" title="Durbar Hall">Durbar Hall</a>, Fateh Prakash Palace Hotel</figcaption></figure>
<p>Udaipur has a diversified economic base. The major contributions to the city's economy come from tourism, agriculture and mineral industries. The handicraft and cottage industry sectors play an important part in contributing to the growing economy.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The city has also been included under the <a href="/wiki/Smart_Cities_in_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Smart Cities in India">Smart Cities</a> mission initiated by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">Government of India</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> and is selected in the list of first 20 cities to be developed as smart cities.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> In the 2001 census of India, 36% of Udaipur resident was reported to be meaningfully employed.
</p>
<dl><dt>Handicrafts</dt></dl>
<p>Udaipur is well known for handicrafts such as paintings, marble articles, silver arts and terracotta. The <a href="/wiki/Shilpgram,_Udaipur" title="Shilpgram, Udaipur">Shilpgram</a> is a platform where regional handicraft and hand-loom products are developed. Craft bazaars are organised by the Shilpgram,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> with an aim to encourage the regional arts and crafts, the handicraft and hand-loom works.
</p>
<dl><dt>Tourism</dt></dl>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:City_Palace_Aerial_View_by_Pranshu_Dubey.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/City_Palace_Aerial_View_by_Pranshu_Dubey.jpg/220px-City_Palace_Aerial_View_by_Pranshu_Dubey.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="159" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/City_Palace_Aerial_View_by_Pranshu_Dubey.jpg/330px-City_Palace_Aerial_View_by_Pranshu_Dubey.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/City_Palace_Aerial_View_by_Pranshu_Dubey.jpg/440px-City_Palace_Aerial_View_by_Pranshu_Dubey.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="866" /></a><figcaption>Aerial view of <a href="/wiki/City_Palace,_Udaipur" title="City Palace, Udaipur">City Palace</a> on <a href="/wiki/Lake_Pichola" title="Lake Pichola">Lake Pichola</a></figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:A_view_of_Villages_and_farms_in_south_Rajasthan_India.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/A_view_of_Villages_and_farms_in_south_Rajasthan_India.jpg/220px-A_view_of_Villages_and_farms_in_south_Rajasthan_India.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/A_view_of_Villages_and_farms_in_south_Rajasthan_India.jpg/330px-A_view_of_Villages_and_farms_in_south_Rajasthan_India.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/A_view_of_Villages_and_farms_in_south_Rajasthan_India.jpg/440px-A_view_of_Villages_and_farms_in_south_Rajasthan_India.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="853" /></a><figcaption>Farming lands amongst the Aravali hills</figcaption></figure>
<p>Udaipur, with its lakes, and historic palaces and architecture, is a major destination for tourists, both domestic and foreign nationals visiting the state. Over 1.4 million tourists visited Udaipur in 2016. With numerous hotels to serve visiting tourists, Udaipur is home to some of the country's most popular luxury hotels and resorts. <a href="/wiki/The_Oberoi_Udaivilas" class="mw-redirect" title="The Oberoi Udaivilas">The Oberoi Udaivilas</a> has been ranked as the world's number 1 hotel in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lake_Palace" title="Lake Palace">The Taj Lake Palace</a> and the Leela Palace Udaipur are also amongst the most expensive hotels in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> With various other renowned hotel chains present in the city, the tourism sector has been a fairly large contributor to the economic growth and fame of Udaipur.
</p>
<dl><dt>Metals and Minerals industries</dt></dl>
<p><a href="/wiki/Udaipur_district" title="Udaipur district">Udaipur district</a> is particularly rich in mineral resources as a large variety of important minerals are found here. Copper, lead, zinc and silver, industrial minerals like phosphate, asbestos, calcite, limestone, Talc (soapstone), barites, wollastonite and marble are the major driving resources behind the industries based in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-dcmsme_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dcmsme-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Marble is exclusively mined, processed and exported from here around the world. The marble industry is well set and established with proper infrastructure and technological support for mining and processing. It is the largest sector giving employment to many people in the city and the immigrants from nearby areas.
Udaipur is also home to the world's second largest Zinc producer, <a href="/wiki/Hindustan_Zinc" title="Hindustan Zinc">Hindustan Zinc</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electronics_design_and_manufacturing">Electronics design and manufacturing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Udaipur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Electronics design and manufacturing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Udaipur is host to medium and large enterprises designing and manufacturing electronic instruments, control panels, sensitive metering technology and LED lamps. The electrical and electronics industry in Udaipur employs over 6,000 people. These businesses are Tempsens, Pyrotech and Secure Meters Ltd.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Secure Meter Limited is one of the major meter manufacturers across the globe.
</p>
<dl><dt>Agriculture</dt></dl>
<p>Agriculture as in most other parts of the country, remains a leading sector in the city's economy. The Major crops of the area are Maize and Jowar in <a href="/wiki/Kharif" class="mw-redirect" title="Kharif">Kharif</a> season and Wheat and Mustard in the <a href="/wiki/Rabi_crop" title="Rabi crop">Rabi</a> season.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Pulses, groundnut and vegetables like brinjals,tomato,bottlegaurd are some of the major food products grown in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Maharana_Pratap_University_of_Agriculture_and_Technology" title="Maharana Pratap University of Agriculture and Technology">Maharana Pratap University of Agriculture and Technology</a>, along with its affiliated institutions, has been working towards identifying, designing, preparing and adapting new techniques in the field of production technology for agricultural development since its establishment.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Udaipur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<td><b><a href="/wiki/City_Palace,_Udaipur" title="City Palace, Udaipur">City Palace, Udaipur</a></b></td>
<td>1559</td>
<td>Standing on the east bank of Lake Pichola is a massive series of palaces built at different times from 1559. Its main entrance is through the triple-arched gate - the Tripolia, built in 1725. This gate leads to a series of courtyards, overlapping partitions, terraces, corridors and gardens. The palace now houses a museum with many antique articles, paintings, decorative furniture and utensils from the royal era - Avijain531
</td></tr>

<td><b><a href="/wiki/Lake_Palace" title="Lake Palace">Lake Palace</a></b></td>
<td>1743–1746</td>
<td>Situated over an island in Lake Pichola, the Lake Palace was constructed to serve as a royal summer palace. Built of white marble, the palace is now a luxury 5 Star hotel, operating under the "<a href="/wiki/Taj_Hotels_Resorts_and_Palaces" class="mw-redirect" title="Taj Hotels Resorts and Palaces">Taj Hotels Resorts and Palaces</a>" banner- Avijain531
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Udaipur,_India,_Jag_Mandir_Palace.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Udaipur%2C_India%2C_Jag_Mandir_Palace.jpg/200px-Udaipur%2C_India%2C_Jag_Mandir_Palace.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Udaipur%2C_India%2C_Jag_Mandir_Palace.jpg/300px-Udaipur%2C_India%2C_Jag_Mandir_Palace.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Udaipur%2C_India%2C_Jag_Mandir_Palace.jpg/400px-Udaipur%2C_India%2C_Jag_Mandir_Palace.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2048" /></a></span></td>
<td><b><a href="/wiki/Jag_Mandir" title="Jag Mandir">Jag Mandir</a></b></td>
<td>1551–1652</td>
<td>Jag Mandir is a palace built on an island in the Lake Pichola. Also known as the "Lake Garden Palace", it was constructed by three Maharanas of the Mewar kingdom. The construction started in 1551 and was completed by 1652. The royal family used the palace as a summer resort and pleasure palace - Avijain531
</td></tr>

</td>
<td>9th century
</td>
<td>
<p>The temple is dedicated to Lord Rishabh dev, the first Jain Tirthankara. The fifty-two pinnacles of the temple are seen from a long distance. The main idol in the temple is of Tirthankara Rishabha, carved in black stone in padmasana posture, about 3.5 feet (1.1&#160;m) tall - Avijain531
</p>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Sajjangarh1.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9c/Sajjangarh1.jpg/200px-Sajjangarh1.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="127" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9c/Sajjangarh1.jpg/300px-Sajjangarh1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9c/Sajjangarh1.jpg/400px-Sajjangarh1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="635" /></a></span></td>
<td><b><a href="/wiki/Monsoon_Palace" title="Monsoon Palace">Monsoon Palace</a></b></td>
<td>-</td>
<td>Monsoon Palace, also known as Sajjan Garh Palace, was built as an astronomical center to keep track of the movement of monsoon clouds in the area and also served as the summer resort of the Maharanas. Built with white marble, it is located on Bansdara peak of the Aravalli hill range at an elevation of 944&#160;m (3100&#160;ft) above mean sea level. The palace has view of the city's lakes, palaces, and surrounding countryside.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Jagdish_Temple_(4).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Jagdish_Temple_%284%29.jpg/200px-Jagdish_Temple_%284%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="142" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Jagdish_Temple_%284%29.jpg/300px-Jagdish_Temple_%284%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Jagdish_Temple_%284%29.jpg/400px-Jagdish_Temple_%284%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4496" data-file-height="3199" /></a></span></td>
<td><b><a href="/wiki/Jagdish_Temple" class="mw-redirect" title="Jagdish Temple">Jagdish Temple</a></b></td>
<td>1651</td>
<td>The <a href="/wiki/Jagdish_Temple" class="mw-redirect" title="Jagdish Temple">Jagdish Temple</a> is a large Hindu temple in the middle of Udaipur, built by Maharana Jagat Singh I. A key tourist place in the city, this temple is an example of <a href="/wiki/M%C4%81ru-Gurjara_architecture" title="Māru-Gurjara architecture">Māru-Gurjara architecture</a>.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Meera_temple_Eklingji.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Meera_temple_Eklingji.jpg/200px-Meera_temple_Eklingji.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="307" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Meera_temple_Eklingji.jpg/300px-Meera_temple_Eklingji.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Meera_temple_Eklingji.jpg/400px-Meera_temple_Eklingji.jpg 2x" data-file-width="748" data-file-height="1147" /></a></span>
</td>
<td><b><a href="/wiki/Eklingji" title="Eklingji">Eklingji</a></b>
</td>
<td>-
</td>
<td>The <a href="/wiki/Eklingji" title="Eklingji">Eklingji Temple</a>, dedicated to Lord Shiva and located 25 kilometers from Udaipur, is one of the most important Hindu pilgrimage sites in Rajasthan. The temple, which is located in the town of Eklingji (Kailashpuri), is the source of the place's common name. Temple is very great and spectacular in idea, as well as in execution, and it is a work of art. The temple's Shikhar towers 50 feet above the ground and has a circumference of 60 feet. A statue of Nandi (bull) facing the deity may be seen on each of the four entrances to the sanctum sanctorum, which has four doors in each of the four directions. It is adorned with a black stone Shiva Lingam with five faces. The ancient temple, which is more than 1300 years old, has a huge campus with up to 72 holy sites, including Samadhis, maths, and temples, spread throughout it.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Lake_Fatehsagar.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Lake_Fatehsagar.jpg/200px-Lake_Fatehsagar.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Lake_Fatehsagar.jpg/300px-Lake_Fatehsagar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Lake_Fatehsagar.jpg/400px-Lake_Fatehsagar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a></span></td>
<td><b><a href="/wiki/Fateh_Sagar_Lake" title="Fateh Sagar Lake">Fateh Sagar Lake</a></b></td>
<td>1678</td>
<td>Lake Fatehsagar is an artificial lake situated in the north-west part of Udaipur. The lake was originally built by Maharana Jai Singh and later reconstructed and extended by Maharana Fateh Singh. It also houses an aquarium named 'Under the Sun' inaugurated in 2017.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Sukhadia_circle,_Udaipur,_Rajasthan.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Sukhadia_circle%2C_Udaipur%2C_Rajasthan.jpg/200px-Sukhadia_circle%2C_Udaipur%2C_Rajasthan.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="112" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Sukhadia_circle%2C_Udaipur%2C_Rajasthan.jpg/300px-Sukhadia_circle%2C_Udaipur%2C_Rajasthan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Sukhadia_circle%2C_Udaipur%2C_Rajasthan.jpg/400px-Sukhadia_circle%2C_Udaipur%2C_Rajasthan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2248" /></a></span></td>
<td><b><a href="/wiki/Sukhadia_Circle" title="Sukhadia Circle">Sukhadia Circle</a></b></td>
<td>-</td>
<td>Sukhadia Circle (square) is large roundabout in the city's northern suburb and is a recreational centre. The square has in its centre, a small pond amidst which lies a 21&#160;ft high three-tiered fountain. The fountain, made of marble is surmounted by a wheat-ear motif, a symbol of prosperity.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Udaipur-Sahelion_Ki_Bari-03-Garden_of_the_rain_without_clouds-20131013.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Udaipur-Sahelion_Ki_Bari-03-Garden_of_the_rain_without_clouds-20131013.jpg/200px-Udaipur-Sahelion_Ki_Bari-03-Garden_of_the_rain_without_clouds-20131013.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Udaipur-Sahelion_Ki_Bari-03-Garden_of_the_rain_without_clouds-20131013.jpg/300px-Udaipur-Sahelion_Ki_Bari-03-Garden_of_the_rain_without_clouds-20131013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Udaipur-Sahelion_Ki_Bari-03-Garden_of_the_rain_without_clouds-20131013.jpg/400px-Udaipur-Sahelion_Ki_Bari-03-Garden_of_the_rain_without_clouds-20131013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="3648" /></a></span></td>
<td><b><a href="/wiki/Saheliyon-ki-Bari" title="Saheliyon-ki-Bari">Saheliyon-ki-Bari</a></b></td>
<td>1710–1734</td>
<td>Sahelion ki Bari is a garden and tourist space in the northern part of the city. The garden with its fountains and kiosks, a lotus pool and marble elephants, was laid for a group of forty-eight young women attendants who accompanied a princess to Udaipur as part of her dowry.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Pichola_See.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Pichola_See.JPG/200px-Pichola_See.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Pichola_See.JPG/300px-Pichola_See.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Pichola_See.JPG/400px-Pichola_See.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a></span></td>
<td><b><a href="/wiki/Lake_Pichola" title="Lake Pichola">Lake Pichola</a></b></td>
<td>1362</td>
<td>Lake Pichola is an artificial freshwater lake and is one of the several contiguous lakes in the city of Udaipur. The lake's surroundings and the several islands within the lake have been developed over the centuries, with palaces, marble temples, family mansions, bathing ghats (<a href="/wiki/Gangaur_Ghat" title="Gangaur Ghat">Gangaur Ghat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ambrai_Ghat" title="Ambrai Ghat">Ambrai Ghat</a>, Hanuman Ghat) and chabutaras (a raised platform, normally within a courtyard).
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Statue_of_Maharana_Pratap_of_Mewar,_commemorating_the_Battle_of_Haldighati,_City_Palace,_Udaipur.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Statue_of_Maharana_Pratap_of_Mewar%2C_commemorating_the_Battle_of_Haldighati%2C_City_Palace%2C_Udaipur.jpg/200px-Statue_of_Maharana_Pratap_of_Mewar%2C_commemorating_the_Battle_of_Haldighati%2C_City_Palace%2C_Udaipur.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="267" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Statue_of_Maharana_Pratap_of_Mewar%2C_commemorating_the_Battle_of_Haldighati%2C_City_Palace%2C_Udaipur.jpg/300px-Statue_of_Maharana_Pratap_of_Mewar%2C_commemorating_the_Battle_of_Haldighati%2C_City_Palace%2C_Udaipur.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Statue_of_Maharana_Pratap_of_Mewar%2C_commemorating_the_Battle_of_Haldighati%2C_City_Palace%2C_Udaipur.jpg/400px-Statue_of_Maharana_Pratap_of_Mewar%2C_commemorating_the_Battle_of_Haldighati%2C_City_Palace%2C_Udaipur.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1600" /></a></span></td>
<td><b><a href="/wiki/Moti_Magri" title="Moti Magri">Moti Magri</a></b></td>
<td>-</td>
<td>Moti Magri or Pearl Hill, is a memorial of the Rajput hero <a href="/wiki/Maharana_Pratap" title="Maharana Pratap">Maharana Pratap</a>. It is basically a small hill, atop of which there is a bronze statue of the Maharana astride his favourite horse "Chetak". It was initiated by Maharana Bhagwat Singh Mewar, and carried over and completed with the help of public trust.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Neemach_Mata_Mandir.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Neemach_Mata_Mandir.jpg/200px-Neemach_Mata_Mandir.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="146" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Neemach_Mata_Mandir.jpg/300px-Neemach_Mata_Mandir.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Neemach_Mata_Mandir.jpg/400px-Neemach_Mata_Mandir.jpg 2x" data-file-width="467" data-file-height="341" /></a></span>

</td>
<td>-
</td>
<td>Neemach mata is located on a hill near Fateh Sagar Lake. The temple is 900 meters above on the top of the hill. This location provides a holistic view of entire Udaipur.
</td></tr>
<tr>

</td></tr>

</td></tr>

(August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> due to the human-sized alphabets reading "I LOVE UDAIPUR", with a view of Lake Pichola and City Palace in the background.
