<td><b><a href="/wiki/Udaisagar_Lake" title="Udaisagar Lake">Udaisagar Lake</a></b>
</td>
<td>1565
</td>
<td>Udai Sagar Lake is one of the five striking lakes situated in Udaipur. Located about 13 kilometres to the east of Udaipur, the construction of this lake was started in 1559 by Maharana Udai Singh. The lake is actually a result of a dam being built on the river Berach to supply adequate water to the Maharana's kingdom. Udai Sagar Lake is 4&#160;km in length, 2.5 kilometres in width and about 9 meters at its deepest.
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Udaipur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mandana_art_work_at_shilpgram.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Mandana_art_work_at_shilpgram.JPG/220px-Mandana_art_work_at_shilpgram.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="154" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Mandana_art_work_at_shilpgram.JPG/330px-Mandana_art_work_at_shilpgram.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Mandana_art_work_at_shilpgram.JPG/440px-Mandana_art_work_at_shilpgram.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3912" data-file-height="2736" /></a><figcaption>Wall painting at <a href="/wiki/Shilpgram,_Udaipur" title="Shilpgram, Udaipur">Shilpgram, Udaipur</a></figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mewari_painting_artist_at_work.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Mewari_painting_artist_at_work.JPG/220px-Mewari_painting_artist_at_work.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Mewari_painting_artist_at_work.JPG/330px-Mewari_painting_artist_at_work.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Mewari_painting_artist_at_work.JPG/440px-Mewari_painting_artist_at_work.JPG 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a><figcaption>Mewari artist at work</figcaption></figure>
<p>Udaipur has a rich cultural heritage from the past e.g. lakes, temples, huge forts, and palaces.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The city has kept a balance between preserving the rituals and traditions of the past while keeping up with the modern advancements and changes in lifestyle{citation needed}. Like any other place in the state of Rajasthan, folk dance and music have an important place in adding to the city's cultural richness. The dynamic and vibrant dances of Bhavai, Ghoomar, Kachchhi Ghodi, Kalbeliya, and Terahtaali add a sparkle to the rich cultural heritage of Udaipur.
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Ghoomar" title="Ghoomar">Ghoomar</a> dance is a part of the Hindu culture of the Mewar Region of Rajasthan. This is a community dance for women and performed on auspicious occasions where the ladies move in circles.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kalbelia" title="Kalbelia">Kalbelia</a>, one of the most sensuous dance forms of Rajasthan, is performed by the Kalbeliya snake charmers' community with the <i>Sapera</i> dancers wearing long, black skirts embroidered with silver ribbons.</li>
<li>Bhavai dance consists of veiled women dancers balancing up to seven or nine brass pitchers as they pirouette and then swaying with the soles of their feet on the top of a glass or on the edge of the sword.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kachchhi_Ghodi_dance" title="Kachchhi Ghodi dance">Kachchhi Ghodi</a> dance is performed on dummy horses where men in elaborate costumes ride the decorated dummy horses. Holding swords, these dancers move to the beating of drums and fifes.<sup id="cite_ref-Art_and_Culture_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Art_and_Culture-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Following a lineage of traditions and religious significance, the various dances complement the fairs and festivals held in the city.  The music consists mainly of the use of morchang, naad, tanpura, and sarangi, among many other instruments.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Miniature paintings are amongst the most famous paintings developed under the patronage of the rulers of <a href="/wiki/Rajasthan" title="Rajasthan">Rajasthan</a>. The simplest among these are done on walls, and through folk in style, they nevertheless have some of the flavors of frescoes one sees in the old palaces. The tradition of painting the wall of houses with scenes from mythological and chivalric tales has been prevalent in Rajasthan for the past many centuries {citation needed}. The people of the city make use of such wall paintings for decorations during wedding celebrations. Noted amongst the miniature style of paintings are particularly the Pichvais, which are those made on cloth, and <a href="/wiki/Phad_painting" title="Phad painting">phad</a>, made on cloth scroll in a folk style.<sup id="cite_ref-Art_and_Culture_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Art_and_Culture-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Bharatiya_Lok_Kala_Mandal" title="Bharatiya Lok Kala Mandal">Bharatiya Lok Kala Mandal</a> is a cultural institution based in the city. The institute with its museum is a platform that displays a collection of <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Rajasthan" title="Culture of Rajasthan">Rajasthani culture</a>. Offering an insight into the lifestyle of the royal era in Udaipur, the museum has a collection of dresses, tribal jewelry, turbans, dolls, masks, musical instruments, paintings, and puppets. With various cultural events including folk song and dance performances, theatre and puppetry, the institute highlights the different social stigmas, thereby proving to be a powerful education tool for the masses.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">Festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Udaipur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Gangaur_Festival">Gangaur Festival</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Udaipur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Gangaur Festival">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Gangaur" title="Gangaur">Gangaur</a> is one of the most important local Hindu festivals in Rajasthan.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> In some form or the other it is celebrated all over Rajasthan.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> "gan" is a synonym for <a href="/wiki/Shiva" title="Shiva">Shiva</a> and "Gauri" or "gaur" stands for Hindu Goddess <a href="/wiki/Parvati" title="Parvati">Parvati</a>, the wife of Shiva. Gangaur celebrates the marriage and is a symbol of conjugal and marital happiness.
</p><p>It is celebrated in the month of <a href="/wiki/Chaitra" title="Chaitra">Chaitra</a> (March–April), the first month of the Hindu calendar. This month marks the end of winter and the onset of spring.
This festival is celebrated by women, who worship clay idols of "Gan" &amp; "Gauri" in their houses. These idols are worshiped by the girls who seek the blessings of Gan and Gauri for a good husband, while the married women pray for the good health and long life of their husbands.
On the eve of the Gangaur festival, women decorate their palms and fingers with henna.
Udaipur has a Ghat named after Gangaur. <a href="/wiki/Gangaur_Ghat" title="Gangaur Ghat">Gangaur Ghat</a> or Gangori Ghat is situated on the waterfront of Lake Pichola. This ghat serves as a location for the celebration of some festivals, including the Gangaur festival. The idols of Gan and Gauri are immersed in the Lake Pichola from this ghat.
</p><p>A traditional procession of Gangaur starts from the City Palace which passes through the city. The procession is headed by old palanquins, chariots, bullock carts, and performance by folk artists.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Shilpgram_Utsav">Shilpgram Utsav</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Udaipur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Shilpgram Utsav">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Shilpgram,_Udaipur" title="Shilpgram, Udaipur">Shilpgram</a>, a crafts village 3&#160; km west of Lake Fateh Sagar, has displays of traditional houses from Rajasthan, Gujarat, Goa, and Maharashtra. There are also demonstrations by musicians, dancers, or artisans from these states. The 10-day festival organized here<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> is a treat for the visitor to an array of exquisite art and craft. One of the important objectives of the Shilpgram festival is in the sphere of increasing awareness and knowledge of rural life and crafts, specifically, for the younger generation. Special emphasis is laid on workshops for children on arts, crafts, theatre, and music.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hariyali_Amavasya">Hariyali Amavasya</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Udaipur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Hariyali Amavasya">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Hariyali Amavasya (new moon day of the Sawan / Shravan month) marks the beginning of the monsoons and greenery. It arrives three days before the famous Hartalika Teej (Shravan Shukla Tritiya). People worship God Shiva for abundant rains and good agricultural season. Melas and fests are arranged in several places in the city.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Jagannath_Rath_Yatra">Jagannath Rath Yatra</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Udaipur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Jagannath Rath Yatra">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In Udaipur, the third biggest <a href="/wiki/Ratha-Yatra" class="mw-redirect" title="Ratha-Yatra">Ratha-Yatra</a><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> is organized on the auspicious day of <a href="/wiki/Ashadh" class="mw-redirect" title="Ashadh">Ashadh</a> Shukla Paksha (bright fortnight) Dwitiya according to Indian <a href="/wiki/Vikram_Samvat" title="Vikram Samvat">Vikram Samvat</a>. On this cultural day of summer solstice theme, June 21 of every year, the journey of the Hindu god Jagannath to aunt's house is started. The presiding Hindu gods of the temple <a href="/wiki/Jagannath" title="Jagannath">Jagannath</a> (<a href="/wiki/Krishna" title="Krishna">Krishna</a>), Balabhadra (<a href="/wiki/Balarama" title="Balarama">Balarama</a>) and their sister <a href="/wiki/Subhadra" title="Subhadra">Subhadra</a> are taken through the streets in decorated wooden chariots, which are made annually. The Chariot of Hindu god Jagannath, called Nandighosha, has 16 wheels and is covered in red and yellow.
</p><p>For many Hindus, the sanctity of the festival is that a touch of the chariot or pulling ropes is considered to give the results of several pious actions or penance for ages.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Jal-Jhulni_Ekadashi">Jal-Jhulni Ekadashi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Udaipur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Jal-Jhulni Ekadashi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>According to the Hindu calendar, Gyaras, or Ekadashi is basically, the 11th day of each waxing (<a href="/wiki/Shukla_paksha" class="mw-redirect" title="Shukla paksha">Shukla paksha</a> ) and waning moon (<a href="/wiki/Krishna_paksha" class="mw-redirect" title="Krishna paksha">Krishna paksha</a>). This Ekadashi, known as Jal-Jhulni Gyaras, or Jal-Jhulni Ekadashi, like all other festivals, is celebrated with enthusiasm.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Udaipur_in_popular_culture">Udaipur in popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Udaipur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Udaipur in popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-halign-center" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:A_dusk_view_of_Lake_Palace_Udaipur_Rajasthan_India.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/A_dusk_view_of_Lake_Palace_Udaipur_Rajasthan_India.jpg/800px-A_dusk_view_of_Lake_Palace_Udaipur_Rajasthan_India.jpg" decoding="async" width="800" height="450" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/A_dusk_view_of_Lake_Palace_Udaipur_Rajasthan_India.jpg/1200px-A_dusk_view_of_Lake_Palace_Udaipur_Rajasthan_India.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/A_dusk_view_of_Lake_Palace_Udaipur_Rajasthan_India.jpg/1600px-A_dusk_view_of_Lake_Palace_Udaipur_Rajasthan_India.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1125" /></a><figcaption><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">Udaipur's Lake Palace at dusk</div></figcaption></figure>
<p>Udaipur was voted the Best City in the World in 2009 by the Travel + Leisure magazine,<sup id="cite_ref-Udaipur_voted_best_city_-_2009_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Udaipur_voted_best_city_-_2009-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> and is now amongst the favourite wedding destinations for Indian as well as foreign nationals.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> The city is a blend of sights, sounds and experiences, which have made it one of the top destinations for weddings and celebrations.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Movies and Television</dt></dl>
<p>Udaipur is mentioned under the spelling <i>Oodeypore</i> in <a href="/wiki/Rudyard_Kipling" title="Rudyard Kipling">Rudyard Kipling</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jungle_Book" title="The Jungle Book">The Jungle Book</a></i> as the birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Bagheera" title="Bagheera">Bagheera</a>, the fictional <a href="/wiki/Leopard" title="Leopard">panther</a> in the king's Menagerie.
</p><p>Because of its scenic locations, Udaipur has been the shooting location for many Hollywood and Bollywood movies. Indian sections of the <a href="/wiki/James_Bond" title="James Bond">James Bond</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Octopussy" title="Octopussy">Octopussy</a></i> were filmed in the city, the Lake Palace, and the Monsoon Palace.  The nearby desert was the backdrop of the remarkable rescue of <a href="/wiki/Octopussy_(character)" class="mw-redirect" title="Octopussy (character)">Octopussy</a> (<a href="/wiki/Maud_Adams" title="Maud Adams">Maud Adams</a>) by Bond (<a href="/wiki/Roger_Moore" title="Roger Moore">Roger Moore</a>). Some scenes from the British television series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jewel_in_the_Crown_(TV_series)" title="The Jewel in the Crown (TV series)">The Jewel in the Crown</a></i> were also filmed in Udaipur.  The Disney channel film, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cheetah_Girls_One_World" class="mw-redirect" title="The Cheetah Girls One World">The Cheetah Girls One World</a></i>, was shot in Udaipur in January 2008. Some of the other non-Indian movies and TV shows filmed in Udaipur include: <i><a href="/wiki/Darjeeling_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="Darjeeling Limited">Darjeeling Limited</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Opening_Night_(1977_film)" title="Opening Night (1977 film)">Opening Night</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Heat_and_Dust_(film)" title="Heat and Dust (film)">Heat and Dust</a></i>, <i>Indische Ring</i>, <i>Inside Octopussy</i>, <i>James Bond in India</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Best_Exotic_Marigold_Hotel" title="The Best Exotic Marigold Hotel">The Best Exotic Marigold Hotel</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Gandhi_(film)" title="Gandhi (film)">Gandhi</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fall_(2006_film)" title="The Fall (2006 film)">The Fall</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Jag_Mandir_(film)" title="Jag Mandir (film)">Jag Mandir</a>, a documentary film directed for television by <a href="/wiki/Werner_Herzog" title="Werner Herzog">Werner Herzog</a> in 1991, was also filmed in the city.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Udaipur has been a location for a number of <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" class="mw-redirect" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a> movies. Some of them shot here include: <i><a href="/wiki/Dhadak" title="Dhadak">Dhadak</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Guide_(film)" title="Guide (film)">Guide</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Mera_Saaya" title="Mera Saaya">Mera Saaya</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Phool_Bane_Angaray" title="Phool Bane Angaray">Phool Bane Angaray</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Kachche_Dhaage" title="Kachche Dhaage">Kachche Dhaage</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Mera_Gaon_Mera_Desh" title="Mera Gaon Mera Desh">Mera Gaon Mera Desh</a></i>, <i>Jalmahal</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Yaadein_(2001_film)" title="Yaadein (2001 film)">Yaadein</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-shooting_locations_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shooting_locations-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> <i>Return of the thief of the bagdad</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Eklavya:_The_Royal_Guard" title="Eklavya: The Royal Guard">Eklavya: The Royal Guard</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dhamaal" title="Dhamaal">Dhamaal</a></i>, <i>Jis Desh Mei Ganga Rehta Hai</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Chalo_Ishq_Ladaaye" title="Chalo Ishq Ladaaye">Chalo Ishq Ladaaye</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Fiza" title="Fiza">Fiza</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Gaddaar_(1995_film)" title="Gaddaar (1995 film)">Gaddaar</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Hum_Hain_Rahi_Pyar_Ke" title="Hum Hain Rahi Pyar Ke">Hum Hain Rahi Pyar Ke</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Khuda_Gawah" title="Khuda Gawah">Khuda Gawah</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Kundan_(film)" title="Kundan (film)">Kundan</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Nandini" title="Nandini">Nandini</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Saajan_Ka_Ghar" title="Saajan Ka Ghar">Saajan Ka Ghar</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Yeh_Jawaani_Hai_Deewani" title="Yeh Jawaani Hai Deewani">Yeh Jawaani Hai Deewani</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pataakha" title="Pataakha">Pataakha</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Mirzya_(film)" title="Mirzya (film)">Mirzya</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Goliyon_Ki_Raasleela_Ram-Leela" title="Goliyon Ki Raasleela Ram-Leela">Goliyon Ki Raasleela Ram-Leela</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-shooting_locations_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shooting_locations-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Prem_Ratan_Dhan_Payo" title="Prem Ratan Dhan Payo">Prem Ratan Dhan Payo</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Love_Aaj_Kal_(2020_film)" title="Love Aaj Kal (2020 film)">Love Aaj Kal</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Angrezi_Medium" title="Angrezi Medium">Angrezi Medium</a></i>. Udaipur is also the setting of various Television series like <i><a href="/wiki/Yeh_Rishta_Kya_Kehlata_Hai" title="Yeh Rishta Kya Kehlata Hai">Yeh Rishta Kya Kehlata Hai</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Rakhi_Ka_Swayamwar" title="Rakhi Ka Swayamwar">Rakhi Ka Swayamwar</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Bharat_Ka_Veer_Putra_%E2%80%93_Maharana_Pratap" title="Bharat Ka Veer Putra – Maharana Pratap">Bharat Ka Veer Putra – Maharana Pratap</a></i>.
</p>
<dl><dt>Events</dt></dl>
<p>Udaipur is a destination for organising various national and international cultural events. Recently, Udaipur hosted the first edition of India's first <a href="/wiki/World_Music_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="World Music Festival">World Music Festival</a>, a two-day festival held on 13 and 14 February 2016. Performances were made by artists and musicians from more than 12 countries, including Spain, Ghana, Venezuela, Italy, France as well as India.<sup id="cite_ref-TheHindu_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheHindu-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
Udaipur is also the host for the Udaipur Lake Festival, a cultural event organized by the <a href="/wiki/Udaipur_Municipal_Corporation" title="Udaipur Municipal Corporation">Udaipur Municipal Corporation</a>. In this festival, Musical programs, adventure sports, jungle safari, bird watching, light and sound shows, art fair etc. are held around the lakes during the three to four day period.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Udaipur is also the host city for the first ASEAN Art camp being organised by the union ministry of external affairs from September 21–29. There are total of 10 countries included and are taking part in the event: Indonesia, Singapore, Malaysia, Philippines, Brunei, Thailand, Cambodia, Myanmar, Vietnam, and India. This 10-day long art camp acts as a platform for cultural and artistic exchange among the participating countries.<sup id="cite_ref-HindustanTimes_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HindustanTimes-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Udaipur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Udaipur is well connected to the major cities of India by land, rail, and air.
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Airport-Udaipur_Terminal.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Airport-Udaipur_Terminal.JPG/220px-Airport-Udaipur_Terminal.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Airport-Udaipur_Terminal.JPG/330px-Airport-Udaipur_Terminal.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Airport-Udaipur_Terminal.JPG/440px-Airport-Udaipur_Terminal.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2176" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Maharana_Pratap_Airport" title="Maharana Pratap Airport">Maharana Pratap Airport</a></figcaption></figure>
<dl><dt>Air</dt></dl>
<p><a href="/wiki/Maharana_Pratap_Airport" title="Maharana Pratap Airport">Maharana Pratap Airport</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> is a small domestic airport situated in a satellite town about 20 kilometres from Udaipur. Daily flights connect Udaipur with <a href="/wiki/Jaipur" title="Jaipur">Jaipur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>,  <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aurangabad_Airport" title="Aurangabad Airport">Aurangabad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kempegowda_International_Airport" title="Kempegowda International Airport">Bangalore</a>,  <a href="/wiki/Rajiv_Gandhi_International_Airport" title="Rajiv Gandhi International Airport">Hyderabad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Surat_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Surat Airport">Surat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lal_Bahadur_Shastri_Airport" title="Lal Bahadur Shastri Airport">Varanasi</a> . <a href="/wiki/Air_India" title="Air India">Air India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vistara" title="Vistara">Vistara</a>, <a href="/wiki/IndiGo" title="IndiGo">IndiGo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spice_Jet" class="mw-redirect" title="Spice Jet">Spice Jet</a> are operational at present. 
</p>
<dl><dt>Rail</dt></dl>
<p><a href="/wiki/Udaipur_City_railway_station" title="Udaipur City railway station">Udaipur City railway station</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rana_Pratap_Nagar_railway_station" title="Rana Pratap Nagar railway station">Rana Pratap Nagar railway station</a> are two railway stations in Udaipur. Through them, Udaipur has direct train connectivity on the broad gauge network to most of the major cities in Rajasthan and the rest of India such as <a href="/wiki/Mysuru" class="mw-redirect" title="Mysuru">Mysuru</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bengaluru" class="mw-redirect" title="Bengaluru">Bengaluru</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khajuraho" title="Khajuraho">Khajuraho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alwar" title="Alwar">Alwar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jaipur" title="Jaipur">Jaipur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kota,_Rajasthan" title="Kota, Rajasthan">Kota</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chittorgarh" title="Chittorgarh">Chittorgarh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ajmer" title="Ajmer">Ajmer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kolkata" title="Kolkata">Kolkata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ratlam" title="Ratlam">Ratlam</a>,<a href="/wiki/Patliputra" class="mw-redirect" title="Patliputra">Patliputra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indore" title="Indore">Indore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ujjain" title="Ujjain">Ujjain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Surat" title="Surat">Surat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vadodara" title="Vadodara">Vadodara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gwalior" title="Gwalior">Gwalior</a> and <a href="/wiki/Agra" title="Agra">Agra</a> and a broad gauge conversion is completed in October 2022 for<a href="/wiki/Ahmedabad" title="Ahmedabad">Ahmedabad</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Luxurious trains, <a href="/wiki/Palace_on_Wheels" title="Palace on Wheels">The Palace on Wheels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Rajasthan_on_Wheels" title="Royal Rajasthan on Wheels">Royal Rajasthan on Wheels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maharaja_Express" class="mw-redirect" title="Maharaja Express">Maharaja Express</a> and The Indian Maharaja have Udaipur as the scheduled stop on their itinerary.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Trains connecting Udaipur with the Capital of India, Delhi include the <a href="/wiki/Mewar_Express" title="Mewar Express">Mewar Express</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chetak_Express" title="Chetak Express">Chetak Express</a>.
</p>
<dl><dt>Road</dt></dl>
<p>The city lies on the intersection point of <a href="/wiki/North-South_and_East-West_Corridor" class="mw-redirect" title="North-South and East-West Corridor">East West Corridor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golden_Quadrilateral" title="Golden Quadrilateral">Golden Quadrilateral</a>, National Highway (NH) 76 and National Highway (NH) 8, midway between <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>, located around 700 kilometres from either city.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/North-South_and_East-West_Corridor" class="mw-redirect" title="North-South and East-West Corridor">East West Corridor</a> which starts from <a href="/wiki/Porbandar" title="Porbandar">Porbandar</a> and ends at <a href="/wiki/Silchar" title="Silchar">Silchar</a> is intersecting the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Quadrilateral" title="Golden Quadrilateral">Golden Quadrilateral</a> and shares the common space from Udaipur to <a href="/wiki/Chittor" class="mw-redirect" title="Chittor">Chittor</a>. The roads in this part of the country are paved and fit for private vehicles. One can either drive from Jaipur (around 6 hours), Ahmedabad (4½ hours) or Surat (9 hours) on NH 8 or Golden Quadrilateral, from Kota (3 hours - EW Corridor or NH 76). <a href="/wiki/Udaipur_City_Bus_Depot" title="Udaipur City Bus Depot">Udaipur City Bus Depot</a> has lines running for the majority of other destinations in Rajasthan and farther north and west towards <a href="/wiki/Madhya_Pradesh" title="Madhya Pradesh">Madhya Pradesh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gujarat" title="Gujarat">Gujarat</a>. Apart from <a href="/wiki/Rajasthan_State_Road_Transport_Corporation" title="Rajasthan State Road Transport Corporation">Rajasthan State Road Transport Corporation</a> (RSRTC), there are numerous private operators and companies providing bus services to and from the other cities.
</p>
<dl><dt>Local transport</dt></dl>
<p>Unmetered taxis, private taxi, radio taxi, auto rickshaws, and regular city bus services are available in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Since 2015 Uber and Ola cab services are available.
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1008px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Lakepalace-udaipur.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Udaipur Panorama from Jag Mandir Island"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Lakepalace-udaipur.jpg/1000px-Lakepalace-udaipur.jpg" decoding="async" width="1000" height="150" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Lakepalace-udaipur.jpg/1500px-Lakepalace-udaipur.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Lakepalace-udaipur.jpg/2000px-Lakepalace-udaipur.jpg 2x" data-file-width="9883" data-file-height="1479" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lakepalace-udaipur.jpg" title="File:Lakepalace-udaipur.jpg"> </a></div>Udaipur Panorama from <a href="/wiki/Jag_Mandir" title="Jag Mandir">Jag Mandir</a> Island</div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Places_nearby">Places nearby</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Udaipur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Places nearby">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourist_attractions_in_Udaipur" class="mw-redirect" title="Tourist attractions in Udaipur">Tourist attractions in Udaipur</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ranakpur_In_India.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Ranakpur_In_India.JPG/220px-Ranakpur_In_India.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Ranakpur_In_India.JPG/330px-Ranakpur_In_India.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Ranakpur_In_India.JPG/440px-Ranakpur_In_India.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1545" data-file-height="1024" /></a><figcaption>The renowned Jain Temple at nearby <a href="/wiki/Ranakpur" title="Ranakpur">Ranakpur</a></figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:A_view_of_Udaipur_Rajasthan_India_March_2015_d.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/A_view_of_Udaipur_Rajasthan_India_March_2015_d.jpg/220px-A_view_of_Udaipur_Rajasthan_India_March_2015_d.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/A_view_of_Udaipur_Rajasthan_India_March_2015_d.jpg/330px-A_view_of_Udaipur_Rajasthan_India_March_2015_d.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/A_view_of_Udaipur_Rajasthan_India_March_2015_d.jpg/440px-A_view_of_Udaipur_Rajasthan_India_March_2015_d.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="853" /></a><figcaption>View of Udaipur from the <a href="/wiki/Monsoon_Palace" title="Monsoon Palace">Monsoon Palace</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>Apart from the local attractions within the city, there are several charming places to see around Udaipur.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Udaipur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Popular sports include cricket, football, hockey, tennis, chess, badminton, archery, etc.
</p>
<dl><dt>Stadiums</dt></dl>
<p>Gandhi Ground is the main sports venue for various events, like athletics, basketball, field hockey, football, Kho Kho and volleyball. <a href="/wiki/Luv_Kush_Indoor_Stadium" title="Luv Kush Indoor Stadium">Luv Kush Indoor Stadium</a> is generally used for the indoor sports especially Badminton and TT.<sup id="cite_ref-stadium_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stadium-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Maharana_Bhupal_Stadium" title="Maharana Bhupal Stadium">Maharana Bhupal Stadium</a> is a multi-purpose stadium used for organising matches of football, cricket and other sports.<sup id="cite_ref-stadium_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stadium-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> For Encouraging Sports in the city and even for encouraging International Sports in the city, a step has been put forward by establishing 'Khel Gaon (village)'or <a href="/wiki/Maharana_Pratap_Khel_Gaon" title="Maharana Pratap Khel Gaon">Maharana Pratap Khel Gaon</a> in Chitrakoot Nagar. It will be committed to 12 sports namely like Basketball, Volleyball, Tennis, Kho-Kho, Kabaddi, Handball, Archery, Rifle shooting, Judo – Karate, Boxing, Swimming, Squash.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Udaipur_International_Cricket_Stadium" title="Udaipur International Cricket Stadium">Udaipur International Cricket Stadium</a> is a proposed cricket stadium in Udaipur.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, after a dispute between <a href="/wiki/Rajasthan_State_Sports_Council" title="Rajasthan State Sports Council">Rajasthan State Sports Council</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rajasthan_Cricket_Association" title="Rajasthan Cricket Association">Rajasthan Cricket Association</a> over the availability of <a href="/wiki/Sawai_Mansingh_Stadium" title="Sawai Mansingh Stadium">Sawai Mansingh Stadium</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Premier_League" title="Indian Premier League">Indian Premier League</a>, the RCA decided to have plans of having their own stadium. RCA has gained land in Udaipur with 9.67 acres from the Udaipur Improvement Trust on a 99-year lease and stadium will have a capacity of 35,000.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Cricket</dt></dl>
<p>Udaipur has several <a href="/wiki/Cricket_Clubs" class="mw-redirect" title="Cricket Clubs">cricket clubs</a> and is home to many state-level players. <a href="/wiki/Ashok_Menaria" title="Ashok Menaria">Ashok Menaria</a> of Udaipur has represented India in U-19 world cup. <a href="/wiki/Ashok_Menaria" title="Ashok Menaria">Ashok Menaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dishant_Yagnik" title="Dishant Yagnik">Dishant Yagnik</a> of the city have played in <a href="/wiki/Indian_Premier_League" title="Indian Premier League">IPL</a> for <a href="/wiki/Rajasthan_Royals" title="Rajasthan Royals">Rajasthan Royals</a>. Rajasthan Royals is a team name of one of the IPL Teams.
</p>
<dl><dt>Chess</dt></dl>
<p><a href="/wiki/Chess" title="Chess">Chess</a> is a popular game in the city among both young and senior players. Udaipur has over 120 International <a href="/wiki/FIDE" title="FIDE">FIDE</a> rated chess players. Players from Udaipur have Represented Rajasthan several times in different Nationals such as Arena Grandmaster Chandrajeet Rajawat. Chandrajeet Rajawat has also won Rajasthan State Championship over seven times in different categories.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Udaipur also has top FIDE rated players of Rajasthan recognized by <a href="/wiki/All_India_Chess_Federation" title="All India Chess Federation">AICF</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Udaipur is also a favourite destination for chess players. With many international chess events throughout the year, bringing more than 1500 players each year from all over the world to compete.
</p>
<dl><dt>Water Sports</dt></dl>
<p>The city's lakes provide an opportunity for water sports. The nearby <a href="/wiki/Dhebar_Lake" title="Dhebar Lake">Jaisamand Lake</a>, situated about 56&#160;km from the city, is equipped with water sports facilities with a range of different boats available.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Kayaking and Canoeing Sports Camps have also been started at the <a href="/wiki/Fateh_Sagar_Lake" title="Fateh Sagar Lake">Fateh Sagar Lake</a>. The city also hosted the 2012 National Kayaking and Canoeing Championship with Fateh Sagar Lake serving as the venue.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Powerlifting</dt></dl>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Asian_Powerlifting_Championships_2016" title="Asian Powerlifting Championships 2016">Asian Powerlifting Championships 2016</a>, organised by <a href="/wiki/Indian_Powerlifting_Federation" title="Indian Powerlifting Federation">Indian Powerlifting Federation</a>, and sanctioned by Asian Powerlifting Federation and <a href="/wiki/International_Powerlifting_Federation" title="International Powerlifting Federation">International Powerlifting Federation</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-invitation_for_2016_power_lifting_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-invitation_for_2016_power_lifting-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> was held in Udaipur from 7 June 2016 to 12 June 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-invitation_for_2016_power_lifting_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-invitation_for_2016_power_lifting-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The city also served as the venue for the Asian Powerlifting Championships in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Udaipur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Schools_in_Udaipur,_Rajasthan" class="mw-redirect" title="Schools in Udaipur, Rajasthan">Schools in Udaipur, Rajasthan</a></div>
<p>Udaipur is home to various government, deemed and private universities. <a href="/wiki/Mohan_Lal_Sukhadia_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Mohan Lal Sukhadia University">Mohan Lal Sukhadia University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maharana_Pratap_University_of_Agriculture_and_Technology" title="Maharana Pratap University of Agriculture and Technology">Maharana Pratap University of Agriculture and Technology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rajiv_Gandhi_Tribal_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Rajiv Gandhi Tribal University">Rajiv Gandhi Tribal University</a> are the major government universities in the city while <a href="/wiki/Janardan_Rai_Nagar_Rajasthan_Vidyapeeth_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Janardan Rai Nagar Rajasthan Vidyapeeth University">J.R.N. Rajasthan Vidyapeeth</a> is a deemed university and <a href="/wiki/Pacific_University" title="Pacific University">Pacific University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bhupal_Nobles_University" title="Bhupal Nobles University">Bhupal Nobles University</a> and SPSU are amongst leading private universities of repute. The <a href="/wiki/Indian_Institute_of_Management_Udaipur" title="Indian Institute of Management Udaipur">Indian Institute of Management Udaipur</a>, established in 2011, also resides in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Udaipur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Newspapers in Udaipur include Hindi dailies <i><a href="/wiki/Rajasthan_Patrika" title="Rajasthan Patrika">Rajasthan Patrika</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dainik_Bhaskar" title="Dainik Bhaskar">Dainik Bhaskar</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Navbharat_Times" title="Navbharat Times">Navbharat Times</a></i>, <i>Apranha Times</i> and <i>Pratahkal</i>. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times_of_India" title="The Times of India">The Times of India</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economic_Times" title="The Economic Times">The Economic Times</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hindustan_Times" class="mw-redirect" title="The Hindustan Times">The Hindustan Times</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hindu" title="The Hindu">The Hindu</a></i> are the English language newspapers circulated in the city.
</p><p>The national, state-owned <a href="/wiki/All_India_Radio" title="All India Radio">All India Radio</a> is broadcast both on the medium wave and FM bands (101.9 MHz) in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Also broadcast in the city there are four private local FM stations: Radio City FM (91.9 MHz), <a href="/wiki/BIG_FM_92.7" class="mw-redirect" title="BIG FM 92.7">Big FM (92.7&#160;MHz)</a>, My FM (94.3 MHz) and Radio Tadka (95 MHz).<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> The public broadcaster <a href="/wiki/Doordarshan" title="Doordarshan">Doordarshan</a> (Prasar Bharati) provides a regional channel besides the mainstay channels.
</p><p>The city is switching over to digitalisation of cable TV as per the third phase of the digitalisation programme by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Information_and_Broadcasting_(India)" title="Ministry of Information and Broadcasting (India)">Ministry of Information and Broadcasting</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
